Jamison Brereton

97 (923)
Plants
Bhiс╣гaj ─Аtharvaс╣Зa
23 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh
Atharvan in character, this hymn is addressed to the healing plants, which are praised for their lineage and their powers and implored to provide remedies for particular sick men. The 1st-person speaker is presumably not merely the poet but also the healer, and he calls on the plants to lend their power to his verbal healing spells (see esp. vs. 14).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI think of the hundred and seven applications of the brown-tinted plural nts, which are ancient, beinggenerated for the gods before the three ages.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ages: dh─Бm─Бni = plural ces to which herbs may be applied by wayof unction, friction, sprinkling etc.; Nirukta, 9.28: either plural ces, names, or births;

Devebhyaс╕е = the shiningseasons;

Triyugam = the three seasons, spring, the rains and autumn

Jamison Brereton

The plants that were born earlier, the third generation before the godsтАФ I shall now call to mind the one hundred and seven forms of those
brown (plants).

HERBS that sprang up in time of old, three ages earlier than the Gods,-
Of these, whose hue is brown, will I declare the hundred powers and seven.

English translation:

тАЬ“plural nts!” thus I hail you, the divine mothers (of mankind). I will give to you, oс╕е physician, a horse, acow, a garment– yes, even myself.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I will give to you: saneyam = dad─Бmi; or, saс╣Гbhajeyam, may I possess;

Puruс╣гa = yaj├▒a puruс╣гa, you whopreside over the sacrifice: Yajus. 12.78

Jamison Brereton

O mothers, called тАЬplants,тАЭ o goddesses, I implore you in this way: тАЬMight I gain a horse, a cow, a garment, (in gaining [=curing]) your
very self, o man.тАЭ

Plants, by this name I speak to you, Mothers, to you the Goddesses:
Steed, cow, and garment may I win, win back thy very self, O man.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour abode is in the A┼Ыvattha, your dwelling is established in the Pal─Б┼Ыa, you are assuredly thedistributer of cattle, inasmuch as you bestow them on the physician.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A┼Ыvattha and Pal─Б┼Ыa: the trees bear achief part in sacrifices and are, therefore, said to be the abode of plural nts. The vessels in which the offerings arepresented are made of the wood of these two trees (Yajus. 12.79). A┼Ыvattha = ficus religiosa;

Pal─Б┼Ыa = buteafrondosa; distributers of cattle: gobh─Бjaс╕е = gav─Бm bh─Бjayitryaс╕е; or, go = ─Аditya, you are partakers of thesun, i.e., plural nts offered to fire or the offering thrown into the fire approaches the sun

Jamison Brereton

Your seat is in the a┼Ыvattha-tree; your nest is made in the parс╣Зa-tree: you will surely get a share in the cow when you will gain [=cure]
the man.

Griffith

The Holy Fig tree is your home, your mansion is the Parna tree:
Winners of cattle shali ye be if ye regain for me this man.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhere, plural nts, you are congregated like princes (assembled) in battle, there the sage is designated aphysician, the destroyer of evil spirits, the extirpator of disease.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the plants have come together, like kings at an assembly,
that inspired poet is said to be a healer who smites the demons and
banishes affliction.

Griffith

He who hath store of Herbs at hand like Kings amid a crowd of men,-
Physician/Vaidya is that Bipra/sage’s name, fiend-slayer, chaser of disease.

Geldner

Bei wem die Kr├дuter sich versammelt haben wie die K├╢nige in der Ratsversammlung, der Redekundige Brahmane hei├Яt Arzt, Unholdt├╢ter, Krankheitsbanner.

Grassmann

Bei wem der Kr├дuter Schar sich trifft, wie F├╝rst und H├дupter in dem Rath, Den nennt man den geschickten Arzt Unhold- und Suchten-B├дndiger.

English translation:

тАЬThe A┼Ыv─Бvat─л, the Som─Бvat─л, the Urjayant─л, the Udojas─Б)– all these plural nts I praise for thepurpose of overcoming this disease.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A┼Ыv─Бvat─л… : these are the four principal plural nts, or, the plural nts, the giver ofhorses (ofr of wealth), the yielder of Soma, the giver of strength (or life), the restorer of vigour; the termsurjayant─л, udojas─Б = tonic and stimulant; for the purpose of overcoming this disease: liс╣н, for this person n for thispreservation

English translation:

тАЬThe virtues of the plural nts which are desirous of bestowing wealth issue from them, man, (towards) yourbody like cattle from the pen.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The unbridled forces of the plants rise up like cows from the cowpen as they seek to gain the stake and your very self, o man.

Griffith

The healing virtues of the Plants stream forth like cattle from the stall,-
Plants that shall win me store of wealth, and save thy vital breath, O man.

Geldner

Die Kr├дfte der Kr├дuter str├╢men aus wie die K├╝he aus dem Kuhstand, die Kr├дuter, die Reichtum gewinnen sollen und dein Leben, o Mann.

Grassmann

Der Kr├дuter D├╝fte str├╢men aus, wie aus dem Stall die Heerde dringt, Um zu gewinnen werthen Preis тАУ und auch dein Leben, lieber Mann.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬVerily Iс╣гkс╣Ыti is your mother, therefore are you (also) Niс╣гkс╣Ыtis; you are flying streams; if (a man) is illyou cure him.тАЭ

Iс╣гkс╣Ыti and Niс╣гkс╣Ыtis: both are synonyms, the unmaker or remedier of disease

causes affliction.

Rivers are ye with wings that fly: keep far whatever brings disease.

English translation:

тАЬThe universal all-pervading plural nts assail (diseases) as a thief (attacks) a cow-shed; they drive outwhatever infirmity of body there may be.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Infirmity: rapaс╕е = p─Бpaс╕е, sin; because of the consequence of sin eitherin this or in a previous existence

Jamison Brereton

They have stepped over the fences like a thief over a barricade.
The plants have driven forth whatever malady of the body there is.

Griffith

Over all fences have they passed, as steals a thief into the fold.
The Plants have driven from the frame whatever malady was there.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs soon as I take these plural nts in my hand making (the sick man) strong, the soul of the maladyperishes before (their application) as (life is driven away from the presence) of the seizer of life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seizer of life: or,as (lives are destroyed) from the seizing of lives, i.e., from the hunting of birds etc.

Jamison Brereton

When I take these plants in my hand, invigorating them,
the very self of the sickness perishes, as if before being captured alive.

Griffith

When, bringing back the vanished strength, I hold these herbs within my hand,
The spirit of disease departs ere he can seize upon the life.

Geldner

Wenn ich nach dem Siegerpreis, dem Gewinn verlangend die Kr├дuter in die Hand nehme, so entweicht der Lebensgeist der Schwindsucht wie vor dem, der lebendig einf├дngt.

Grassmann

Wenn ich, ihr Arzeneien, euch in meine H├дnde drohend fass’, So macht das Siechthum sich davon, es bangt ihm vor des H├дschers Griff.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ рдУрд╖рдзрдпрдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд░реБрдЧреНрдгрд╕реНрдп рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрдордЩреНрдЧрдВ рдпрджреНрдпрджрдЩреНрдЧрдВ рдкрд░реБрдГрдкрд░реБрдГ рдпрджреНрдпрддреНрдкрд░реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд░реНрдкрде рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрде рддрддрдГ рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рддреНрдкрд░реНрд╡рдгрд╢реНрдЪ рдпрдХреНрд╖реНрдордВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдзрд┐рдВ рд╡рд┐ рдмрд╛рдзрдзреНрд╡реЗ ред рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ рдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгрдмрд▓рдГ рдордзреНрдпрдорд╢реАрдГ рдордзреНрдпрдорд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдиреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рдЙрдкрджреНрд░рд╡рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдГ рд╕рдордирдиреНрддрд░рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдкрджреЗ рдкрджреЗ рд╡рд┐рдмрд╛рдзрддреЗ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFrom him, oс╕е plural nts, in whom you creep from limb to limb, from joint to joint, you drive away diseaselike a mighty (prince) stationed in the midst of his host.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mighty prince: or, as Rudra pierces the world with thecentral point of his trident (Yajus. 12.86)

Jamison Brereton

Him whose every limb, every joint you slither over,
from him thrust aside the sickness, like a mighty (man) lying in the middle.

Griffith

He through whose frame, O Plants, ye creep member by member, joint by joint,-
From him ye drive away disease like some strong arbiter of strife.

Geldner

Bei wem ihr Kr├дuter Glied um Glied, Gelenk um Gelenk vordringt, von dem vertreibt ihr die Schwindsucht, wie ein M├дchtiger, der in der Mitte zwischen zwei Freunden lagert.

Grassmann

Auf eurem Weg von Glied zu Glied, und von Gelenke zu Gelenk Treibt ihr das Siechthum vor euch her, als w├дr’s durch strengen Richters Spruch.

Elizarenkova

тАЬFly forth, sickness, with the jay, with the blue jay, with the velocity of the wind, perish along with theiguana.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Iguana: kikid─лvin─Б: an epithet of c─Бс╣гeс╣Зa, making these kiki; perhaps, an allusion to the severaldiseases arising from vitiated bile, phlegm and wind (Yajuс╣г)

blizzard [?].

English translation:

тАЬLet each of you, plural nts, go to the other, approach the one (to the vicinity) of the other; thus being allmutually joined together, attend to this my speech.тАЭ

All of you, being in agreementтАФhelp this speech of mine.

All of you be accordant, give furtherance to this speech of mine.

Von euch sei eins dem andern hold und jedes helf dem andern aus; Seid eines Sinnes allzumal und folget diesem meinem Wort.

тАЬThe plural nts, falling from heaven, said, “The man, whom living we pervade, will not perish”.тАЭ

Flying down from heaven, the plants spoke:
тАЬThe man whom we will reach (while he is still) alive, that man will not suffer harm.тАЭ

Griffith

What time, descending from the sky, the Plants flew earthward, thus they spake:
No evil shall befall the man whom while he liveth we pervade,

English translation:

тАЬThe which have the Soma for their king, and are numerous and all- seeking of them you (O Soma) arethe best; be very bountiful to the affectionate heart.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The many plants, having a hundred appearances, whose king
is SomaтАФ
of those you are the highestтАФsufficient for our desire, weal for our heart.

Griffith

Of all the many Plants whose King is, Soma, Plants of hundred forms,
Thou art the Plant most excellent, prompt to the wish, sweet to the heart.

Die vielen Kr├дuter unter K├╢nig Soma, von hundertfachem Aussehen, deren oberstes bist du, recht nach Wunsch, dem Herzen wohltuend.

Der Kr├дuter in des Soma Reich, der vielen hundertfach an Art, All dieser bist das beste du, dem Wunsche recht, dem Herzen hold.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet not the digger hurt you, not (the sick person n) for whom I dig you up; may all my bipeds andquadrupeds be free from disease.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let your digger not suffer harm, nor him for whom I dig you.
Let our two-footed and four-footed all be free of affliction.

Griffith

Unharmed be he who digs you up, unharmed the man for whom I dig:
And let no malady attack biped or quadruped of ours.

Geldner

Nicht soll der Schaden leiden, der euch gr├дbt, noch der, f├╝r den ich euch grabe. Unsere Zweif├╝├Яler und Vierf├╝├Яler sollen alle gesund sein.

Grassmann

Nicht nehme Schaden wer euch gr├дbt, noch der, f├╝r den ich grabe euch; Was zwei und was vier F├╝sse hat, das bleibe alles uns gesund.

all of you, having coming together, o sproutsтАФjointly give heroic power to this one here [=medicinal plant].

Come all assembled and confer your healing power upon this Herb.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou (Soma) are the best of the plural nts, to you (all) trees are prostrate; may he be prostrate to us, whoattacks us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May the trees shelter you, and may he who is our foe become our own servant

Jamison Brereton

You are the highest, o plant. The trees are your subordinates.
Let him be subordinate to us, whoever assails us.

Griffith

Most excellent of all art thou, O Plant thy vassals are the trees.
Let him be subject to our power, the man who seeks to injure us.

Geldner

Du Kraut, bist das Oberste, die B├дume sind deine Untergebenen. Der soll unser Untergebener sein, der uns bedroht!

Grassmann

O Kraut, du bist der Oberherr; die B├дume sind dir unterthan; Und so sei uns auch unterthan der, welcher uns zu schaden sucht.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдУрд╖рдзреЗ рддреНрд╡рдореН-рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╛-рдЕрд╕рд┐) рд╣реЗ рдУрд╖рдзреЗ ! рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛рд╜рд╕рд┐ (рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдГ-рддрд╡-рдЙрдкрд╕реНрддрдпрдГ) рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдГ рдмреГрд╣рддреНрддрд░рд╡рд╕реНрддрд╡ рдЦрд▓реВрдкрд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ тАЬрдЙрдкрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╕реНрддреНрдпреИ рд╕рдЩреНрдШрд╛рддреЗтАЭ [рднреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐реж] тАЬрдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рд░рдгрдВ рдЪтАЭ (рд╕рдГ-рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН-рдЙрдкрд╕реНрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ) рд╕ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рднрд┐рд╖рдХреН рдЦрд▓реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореБрдкрд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрджрд╛рддрд╛ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреЛ рднрд╡рддреБ (рдпрдГ-рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН-рдЕрднрд┐рджрд╛рд╕рддрд┐) рдпреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдереНрдпрд╕реБрдЦрдорднрд┐рджрджрд╛рддрд┐ тАЬрджрд╛рд╕рддрд┐ рджрд╛рдирдХрд░реНрдорд╛тАЭ [рдирд┐рдШреж рейредреиреж] реереирейрее
